If this is empty, all resources for the API are\\n75:   // returned. LDS/CDS may have empty ``resource_names``, which will cause all\\n76:   // resources for the Envoy instance to be returned. The LDS and CDS responses\\n77:   // will then imply a number of resources that need to be fetched via EDS/RDS,\\n78:   // which will be explicitly enumerated in ``resource_names``.\\n79:   repeated string resource_names = 3;\\n80: \\n81:   // [#not-implemented-hide:]\\n82:   // Alternative to ``resource_names`` field that allows specifying dynamic\\n83:   // parameters along with each resource name. Clients that populate this\\n84:   // field must be able to handle responses from the server where resources\\n85:   // are wrapped in a Resource message.\\n86:   //\\n87:   // .. note::\\n88:   //   It is legal for a request to have some resources listed\\n89:   //   in ``resource_names`` and others in ``resource_locators``.\\n90:   //\\n91:   repeated ResourceLocator resource_locators = 7;\\n92: \\n93:   // Type of the resource that is being requested, e.g.\\n94:   // ``type.googleapis.com/envoy.api.v2.ClusterLoadAssignment``. This is implicit\\n95:   // in requests made via singleton xDS APIs such as CDS, LDS, etc. but is\\n96:   // required for ADS.\\n97:   string type_url = 4;\\n98: \\n99:   // nonce corresponding to ``DiscoveryResponse`` being ACK/NACKed. See above\\n100:   // discussion on ``version_info`` and the ``DiscoveryResponse`` nonce comment. This\\n101:   // may be empty only if:\\n102:   //\\n103:   // * This is a non-persistent-stream xDS such as HTTP, or\\n104:   // * The client has not yet accepted an update in this xDS stream (unlike\\n105:   //   delta, where it is populated only for new explicit ACKs).\\n106:   //\\n107:   string response_nonce = 5;\\n108: \\n109:   // This is populated when the previous :ref:`DiscoveryResponse <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.discovery.v3.DiscoveryResponse>`\\n110:   // failed to update configuration. The ``message`` field in ``error_details`` provides the Envoy\\n111:   // internal exception related to the failure. It is only intended for consumption during manual\\n112:   // debugging, the string provided is not guaranteed to be stable across Envoy versions.\\n113:   google.rpc.Status error_detail = 6;\\n114: }\\n115: \\n116: // [#next-free-field: 8]\\n117: message DiscoveryResponse {\\n118:   option (udpa.annotations.versioning).previous_message_type = \\\"envoy.api.v2.DiscoveryResponse\\\";\\n119: \\n120:   // The version of the response data.\\n121:   string version_info = 1;\\n122: \\n123:   // The response resources. These resources are typed and depend on the API being called.\\n124:   repeated google.protobuf.Any resources = 2;\\n125: \\n126:   // [#not-implemented-hide:]\\n127:   // Canary is used to support two Envoy command line flags:\\n128:   //\\n129:   // * ``--terminate-on-canary-transition-failure``. When set, Envoy is able to\\n130:   //   terminate if it detects that configuration is stuck at canary. Consider\\n131:   //   this example sequence of updates:\\n132:   //\\n133:   //   * Management server applies a canary config successfully.\\n134:   //   * Management server rolls back to a production config.\\n135:   //   * Envoy rejects the new production config.\\n136:   //\\n137:   //   Since there is no sensible way to continue receiving configuration\\n138:   //   updates, Envoy will then terminate and apply production config from a\\n139:   //   clean slate.\\n140:   //\\n141:   // * ``--dry-run-canary``. When set, a canary response will never be applied, only\\n142:   //   validated via a dry run.\\n143:   //\\n144:   bool canary = 3;\\n145: \\n146:   // Type URL for resources. Identifies the xDS API when muxing over ADS.\\n147:   // Must be consistent with the ``type_url`` in the 'resources' repeated Any (if non-empty).\\n148:   string type_url = 4;\\n149: \\n150:   // For gRPC based subscriptions, the nonce provides a way to explicitly ack a\\n151:   // specific ``DiscoveryResponse`` in a following ``DiscoveryRequest``. Additional\\n152:   // messages may have been sent by Envoy to the management server for the\\n153:   // previous version on the stream prior to this ``DiscoveryResponse``, that were\\n154:   // unprocessed at response send time. The nonce allows the management server\\n155:   // to ignore any further ``DiscoveryRequests`` for the previous version until a\\n156:   // ``DiscoveryRequest`` bearing the nonce. The nonce is optional and is not\\n157:   // required for non-stream based xDS implementations.\\n158:   string nonce = 5;\\n159: \\n160:   // The control plane instance that sent the response.\\n161:   config.core.v3.ControlPlane control_plane = 6;\\n162: \\n163:   // [#not-implemented-hide:]\\n164:   // Errors associated with specific resources. Clients are expected to\\n165:   // remember the most recent error for a given resource across responses;\\n166:   // the error condition is not considered to be cleared until a response is\\n167:   // received that contains the resource in the 'resources' field.\\n168:   repeated ResourceError resource_errors = 7;\\n169: }\\n170: \\n171: // DeltaDiscoveryRequest and DeltaDiscoveryResponse are used in a new gRPC\\n172: // endpoint for Delta xDS.\\n173: //\\n174: // With Delta xDS, the DeltaDiscoveryResponses do not need to include a full\\n175: // snapshot of the tracked resources. Instead, DeltaDiscoveryResponses are a\\n176: // diff to the state of a xDS client.\\n177: // In Delta XDS there are per-resource versions, which allow tracking state at\\n178: // the resource granularity.\\n179: // An xDS Delta session is always in the context of a gRPC bidirectional\\n180: // stream. This allows the xDS server to keep track of the state of xDS clients\\n181: // connected to it.\\n182: //\\n183: // In Delta xDS the nonce field is required and used to pair\\n184: // ``DeltaDiscoveryResponse`` to a ``DeltaDiscoveryRequest`` ACK or NACK.\\n185: // Optionally, a response message level ``system_version_info`` is present for\\n186: // debugging purposes only.\\n187: //\\n188: // ``DeltaDiscoveryRequest`` plays two independent roles. Any ``DeltaDiscoveryRequest``\\n189: // can be either or both of:\\n190: //\\n191: // * Informing the server of what resources the client has gained/lost interest in\\n192: //   (using ``resource_names_subscribe`` and ``resource_names_unsubscribe``), or\\n193: // * (N)ACKing an earlier resource update from the server (using ``response_nonce``,\\n194: //   with presence of ``error_detail`` making it a NACK).\\n195: //\\n196: // Additionally, the first message (for a given ``type_url``) of a reconnected gRPC stream\\n197: // has a third role: informing the server of the resources (and their versions)\\n198: // that the client already possesses, using the ``initial_resource_versions`` field.\\n199: //\\n200: // As with state-of-the-world, when multiple resource types are multiplexed (ADS),\\n201: // all requests/acknowledgments/updates are logically walled off by ``type_url``:\\n202: // a Cluster ACK exists in a completely separate world from a prior Route NACK.\\n203: // In particular, ``initial_resource_versions`` being sent at the \\\"start\\\" of every\\n204: // gRPC stream actually entails a message for each ``type_url``, each with its own\\n205: // ``initial_resource_versions``.\\n206: // [#next-free-field: 10]\\n207: message DeltaDiscoveryRequest {\\n208:   option (udpa.annotations.versioning).previous_message_type = \\\"envoy.api.v2.DeltaDiscoveryRequest\\\";\\n209: \\n210:   // The node making the request.\\n211:   config.core.v3.Node node = 1;\\n212: \\n213:   // Type of the resource that is being requested, e.g.\\n214:   // ``type.googleapis.com/envoy.api.v2.ClusterLoadAssignment``. This does not need to be set if\\n215:   // resources are only referenced via ``xds_resource_subscribe`` and\\n216:   // ``xds_resources_unsubscribe``.\\n217:   string type_url = 2;\\n218: \\n219:   // DeltaDiscoveryRequests allow the client to add or remove individual\\n220:   // resources to the set of tracked resources in the context of a stream.\\n221:   // All resource names in the ``resource_names_subscribe`` list are added to the\\n222:   // set of tracked resources and all resource names in the ``resource_names_unsubscribe``\\n223:   // list are removed from the set of tracked resources.\\n224:   //\\n225:   // *Unlike* state-of-the-world xDS, an empty ``resource_names_subscribe`` or\\n226:   // ``resource_names_unsubscribe`` list simply means that no resources are to be\\n227:   // added or removed to the resource list.\\n228:   // *Like* state-of-the-world xDS, the server must send updates for all tracked\\n229:   // resources, but can also send updates for resources the client has not subscribed to.\\n230:   //\\n231:   // .. note::\\n232:   //   The server must respond with all resources listed in ``resource_names_subscribe``,\\n233:   //   even if it believes the client has the most recent version of them. The reason:\\n234:   //   the client may have dropped them, but then regained interest before it had a chance\\n235:   //   to send the unsubscribe message. See DeltaSubscriptionStateTest.RemoveThenAdd.\\n236:   //\\n237:   // These two fields can be set in any ``DeltaDiscoveryRequest``, including ACKs\\n238:   // and ``initial_resource_versions``.\\n239:   //\\n240:   // A list of Resource names to add to the list of tracked resources.\\n241:   repeated string resource_names_subscribe = 3;\\n242: \\n243:   // A list of Resource names to remove from the list of tracked resources.\\n244:   repeated string resource_names_unsubscribe = 4;\\n245: \\n246:   // [#not-implemented-hide:]\\n247:   // Alternative to ``resource_names_subscribe`` field that allows specifying dynamic parameters\\n248:   // along with each resource name.\\n249:   //\\n250:   // .. note::\\n251:   //   It is legal for a request to have some resources listed\\n252:   //   in ``resource_names_subscribe`` and others in ``resource_locators_subscribe``.\\n253:   //\\n254:   repeated ResourceLocator resource_locators_subscribe = 8;\\n255: \\n256:   // [#not-implemented-hide:]\\n257:   // Alternative to ``resource_names_unsubscribe`` field that allows specifying dynamic parameters\\n258:   // along with each resource name.\\n259:   //\\n260:   // .. note::\\n261:   //   It is legal for a request to have some resources listed\\n262:   //   in ``resource_names_unsubscribe`` and others in ``resource_locators_unsubscribe``.\\n263:   //\\n264:   repeated ResourceLocator resource_locators_unsubscribe = 9;\\n265: \\n266:   // Informs the server of the versions of the resources the xDS client knows of, to enable the\\n267:   // client to continue the same logical xDS session even in the face of gRPC stream reconnection.\\n268:   // It will not be populated:\\n269:   //\\n270:   // * In the very first stream of a session, since the xDS client.\\n276:   // The map's values are opaque resource versions.\\n277:   map<string, string> initial_resource_versions = 5;\\n278: \\n279:   // When the ``DeltaDiscoveryRequest`` is a ACK or Additional\\n152:   // messages may have been sent by Envoy to the management server for the\\n153:   // previous version on the stream prior to this ``DiscoveryResponse``, that were\\n154:   // unprocessed at response send time. The nonce allows the management server\\n155:   // to ignore any further ``DiscoveryRequests`` for the previous version until a\\n156:   // ``DiscoveryRequest`` bearing the nonce. The nonce is optional and is not\\n157:   // required for non-stream based xDS implementations.\\n158:   string nonce = 5;\\n159: \\n160:   // The control plane instance that sent the response.\\n161:   config.core.v3.ControlPlane control_plane = 6;\\n162: \\n163:   // [#not-implemented-hide:]\\n164:   // Errors associated with specific resources. Clients are expected to\\n165:   // remember the most recent error for a given resource across responses;\\n166:   // the error condition is not considered to be cleared until a response is\\n167:   // received that contains the resource in the 'resources' field.\\n168:   repeated ResourceError resource_errors = 7;\\n169: }\\n170: \\n171: // DeltaDiscoveryRequest and DeltaDiscoveryResponse are used in a new gRPC\\n172: // endpoint for Delta xDS.\\n173: //\\n174: // With Delta xDS, the DeltaDiscoveryResponses do not need to include a full\\n175: // snapshot of the tracked resources. Instead, DeltaDiscoveryResponses are a\\n176: // diff to the state of a xDS client.\\n177: // In Delta XDS there are per-resource versions, which allow tracking state at\\n178: // the resource granularity.\\n179: // An xDS Delta session is always in the context of a gRPC bidirectional\\n180: // stream. This allows the xDS server to keep track of the state of xDS clients\\n181: // connected to it.\\n182: //\\n183: // In Delta xDS the nonce field is required and used to pair\\n184: // ``DeltaDiscoveryResponse`` to a ``DeltaDiscoveryRequest`` ACK or NACK.\\n185: // Optionally, a response message level ``system_version_info`` is present for\\n186: // debugging purposes only.\\n187: //\\n188: // ``DeltaDiscoveryRequest`` plays two independent roles. Any ``DeltaDiscoveryRequest``\\n189: // can be either or both of:\\n190: //\\n191: // * Informing the server of what resources the client has gained/lost interest in\\n192: //   (using ``resource_names_subscribe`` and ``resource_names_unsubscribe``), or\\n193: // * (N)ACKing an earlier resource update from the server (using ``response_nonce``,\\n194: //   with presence of ``error_detail`` making it a NACK).\\n195: //\\n196: // Additionally, the first message (for a given ``type_url``) of a reconnected gRPC stream\\n197: // has a third role: informing the server of the resources (and their versions)\\n198: // that the client already possesses, using the ``initial_resource_versions`` field.\\n199: //\\n200: // As with state-of-the-world, when multiple resource types are multiplexed (ADS),\\n201: // all requests/acknowledgments/updates are logically walled off by ``type_url``:\\n202: // a Cluster ACK exists in a completely separate world from a prior Route NACK.\\n203: // In particular, ``initial_resource_versions`` being sent at the \\\"start\\\" of every\\n204: // gRPC stream actually entails a message for each ``type_url``, each with its own\\n205: // ``initial_resource_versions``.\\n206: // [#next-free-field: 10]\\n207: message DeltaDiscoveryRequest {\\n208:   option (udpa.annotations.versioning).previous_message_type = \\\"envoy.api.v2.DeltaDiscoveryRequest\\\";\\n209: \\n210:   // The node making the request.\\n211:   config.core.v3.Node node = 1;\\n212: \\n213:   // Type of the resource that is being requested, e.g.\\n214:   // ``type.googleapis.com/envoy.api.v2.ClusterLoadAssignment``. This does not need to be set if\\n215:   // resources are only referenced via ``xds_resource_subscribe`` and\\n216:   // ``xds_resources_unsubscribe``.\\n217:   string type_url = 2;\\n218: \\n219:   // DeltaDiscoveryRequests allow the client to add or remove individual\\n220:   // resources to the set of tracked resources in the context of a stream.\\n221:   // All resource names in the ``resource_names_subscribe`` list are added to the\\n222:   // set of tracked resources and all resource names in the ``resource_names_unsubscribe``\\n223:   // list are removed from the set of tracked resources.\\n224:   //\\n225:   // *Unlike* state-of-the-world xDS, an empty ``resource_names_subscribe`` or\\n226:   // ``resource_names_unsubscribe`` list simply means that no resources are to be\\n227:   // added or removed to the resource list.\\n228:   // *Like* state-of-the-world xDS, the server must send updates for all tracked\\n229:   // resources, but can also send updates for resources the client has not subscribed to.\\n230:   //\\n231:   // .. note::\\n232:   //   The server must respond with all resources listed in ``resource_names_subscribe``,\\n233:   //   even if it believes the client has the most recent version of them. The reason:\\n234:   //   the client may have dropped them, but then regained interest before it had a chance\\n235:   //   to send the unsubscribe message. See DeltaSubscriptionStateTest.RemoveThenAdd.\\n236:   //\\n237:   // These two fields can be set in any ``DeltaDiscoveryRequest``, including ACKs\\n238:   // and ``initial_resource_versions``.\\n239:   //\\n240:   // A list of Resource names to add to the list of tracked resources.\\n241:   repeated string resource_names_subscribe = 3;\\n242: \\n243:   // A list of Resource names to remove from the list of tracked resources.\\n244:   repeated string resource_names_unsubscribe = 4;\\n245: \\n246:   // [#not-implemented-hide:]\\n247:   // Alternative to ``resource_names_subscribe`` field that allows specifying dynamic parameters\\n248:   // along with each resource name.\\n249:   //\\n250:   // .. note::\\n251:   //   It is legal for a request to have some resources listed\\n252:   //   in ``resource_names_subscribe`` and others in ``resource_locators_subscribe``.\\n253:   //\\n254:   repeated ResourceLocator resource_locators_subscribe = 8;\\n255: \\n256:   // [#not-implemented-hide:]\\n257:   // Alternative to ``resource_names_unsubscribe`` field that allows specifying dynamic parameters\\n258:   // along with each resource name.\\n259:   //\\n260:   // .. note::\\n261:   //   It is legal for a request to have some resources listed\\n262:   //   in ``resource_names_unsubscribe`` and others in ``resource_locators_unsubscribe``.\\n263:   //\\n264:   repeated ResourceLocator resource_locators_unsubscribe = 9;\\n265: \\n266:   // Informs the server of the versions of the resources the xDS client knows of, to enable the\\n267:   // client to continue the same logical xDS session even in the face of gRPC stream reconnection.\\n268:   // It will not be populated:\\n269:   //\\n270:   // * In the very first stream of a session, since the client will not yet have any resources.\\n271:   // * In any message after the first in a stream (for a given ``type_url``), since the server will\\n272:   //   already be correctly tracking the client's state.\\n273:   //\\n274:   // (In ADS, the first message ``of each type_url`` of a reconnected stream populates this map.)\\n275:   // The map's keys are names of xDS resources known to the xDS client.\\n276:   // The map's values are opaque resource versions.\\n277:   map<string, string> initial_resource_versions = 5;\\n278: \\n279:   // When the ``DeltaDiscoveryRequest`` is a ACK or NACK message in response\\n280:   // to a previous ``DeltaDiscoveryResponse``, the ``response_nonce`` must be the\\n281:   // nonce in the ``DeltaDiscoveryResponse``.\\n282:   // Otherwise (unlike in ``DiscoveryRequest``) ``response_nonce`` must be omitted.\\n283:   string response_nonce = 6;\\n284: \\n285:   // This is populated when the previous :ref:`DiscoveryResponse <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.discovery.v3.DiscoveryResponse>`\\n286:   // failed to update configuration. The ``message`` field in ``error_details``\\n287:   // provides the Envoy internal exception related to the failure.\\n288:   google.rpc.Status error_detail = 7;\\n289: }\\n290: \\n291: // [#next-free-field: 10]\\n292: message DeltaDiscoveryResponse {\\n293:   option (udpa.annotations.versioning).previous_message_type =\\n294:       \\\"envoy.api.v2.DeltaDiscoveryResponse\\\";\\n295: \\n296:   // The version of the response data (used for debugging).\\n297:   string system_version_info = 1;\\n298: \\n299:   // The response resources. These are typed resources, whose types must match\\n300:   // the ``type_url`` field.\\n301:   repeated Resource resources = 2;\\n302: \\n303:   // field id 3 IS available!\\n304: \\n305:   // Type URL for resources. Identifies the xDS API when muxing over ADS.\\n306:   // Must be consistent with the ``type_url`` in the Any within 'resources' if 'resources' is non-empty.\\n307:   string type_url = 4;\\n308: \\n309:   // Resource names of resources that have been deleted and to be removed from the xDS Client.\\n310:   // Removed resources for missing resources can be ignored.\\n311:   repeated string removed_resources = 6;\\n312: \\n313:   // Alternative to ``removed_resources`` that allows specifying which variant of\\n314:   // a resource is being removed. be other clients that need\\n360:       // special configuration based on that key.\\n361:       Exists exists = 3;\\n362:     }\\n363:   }\\n364: \\n365:   message ConstraintList {\\n366:     // A list of constraints that match if any one constraint in the list\\n374:     // matches.\\n375:     ConstraintList or_constraints = 2;\\n376: \\n377:     // A list of constraints that must all match.\\n378:     ConstraintList and_constraints = 3;\\n379: \\n380:     // The inverse (NOT) of a set of constraints.\\n381:     DynamicParameterConstraints not_constraints = 4;\\n382:   }\\n383: }\\n384: \\n385: // [#next-free-field: 10]\\n386: message Resource {\\n387:   option (udpa.annotations.versioning).previous_message_type = \\\"envoy.api.v2.Resource\\\";\\n388: \\n389:   // Cache The data plane sends to the service information about the HTTP request.\\n30: // 2. The service sends back a ``ProcessingResponse`` message that directs the data plane to either\\n31: //    stop processing, continue without it, or send it the next chunk of the message body.\\n32: // 3. If so requested, the data plane sends the server the message body in chunks, or the entire\\n33: //    body at once. In either case, the server may send back a ``ProcessingResponse`` for each\\n34: //    message it receives, or wait for a certain amount of body chunks to be received before\\n35: //    streaming back the ``ProcessingResponse`` messages.\\n36: // 4. If so requested, the data plane sends the server the HTTP trailers, and the server sends back\\n37: //    a ``ProcessingResponse``.\\n38: // 5. At this point, request processing is done, and we pick up again at step 1 when the data plane\\n39: //    receives a response from the upstream server.\\n40: // 6. At any point above, if the server closes the gRPC stream cleanly, then the data plane\\n41: //    proceeds without consulting the server.\\n42: // 7. At any point above, if the server closes the gRPC stream with an error, then the data plane\\n43: //    returns a ``500`` error to the client, unless the filter was configured to ignore errors.\\n44: //\\n45: // In other words, the process is a request/response conversation, but using a gRPC stream to make\\n46: // it easier for the server to maintain state.\\n47: service ExternalProcessor {\\n48:   // This begins the bidirectional stream that the data plane will use to\\n49:   // give the server control over what the filter does. The actual\\n50:   // protocol is described by the ``ProcessingRequest`` and ``ProcessingResponse``\\n51:   // messages below.\\n52:   rpc Process(stream ProcessingRequest) returns (stream ProcessingResponse) {\\n53:   }\\n54: }\\n55: \\n56: // This message specifies the filter protocol configurations which will be sent to the ext_proc\\n57: // server in a :ref:`ProcessingRequest <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingRequest>`.\\n58: // If the server does not support these protocol configurations, it may choose to close the gRPC\\n59: // stream. If the server supports these protocol configurations, it should respond based on the\\n60: // API specifications.\\n61: message ProtocolConfiguration {\\n62:   // Specifies the filter configuration\\n63:   // :ref:`request_body_mode <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingMode.request_body_mode>`.\\n64:   envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingMode.BodySendMode request_body_mode = 1\\n65:       [(validate.rules).enum = {defined_only: true}];\\n66: \\n67:   // Specifies the filter configuration\\n68:   // :ref:`response_body_mode <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingMode.response_body_mode>`.\\n69:   envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingMode.BodySendMode response_body_mode = 2\\n70:       [(validate.rules).enum = {defined_only: true}];\\n71: \\n72:   // Specifies the filter configuration\\n73:   // :ref:`send_body_without_waiting_for_header_response <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.send_body_without_waiting_for_header_response>`.\\n74:   // If the client is waiting for a header response from the server, setting to ``true`` means the\\n75:   // client will send the body to the server as it arrives. Setting to ``false`` means the client\\n76:   // will buffer the arrived data and not send it to the server immediately.\\n77:   bool send_body_without_waiting_for_header_response = 3;\\n78: }\\n79: \\n80: // This represents the different types of messages that the data plane can send\\n81: // to an external processing server.\\n82: // [#next-free-field: 12]\\n83: message ProcessingRequest {\\n84:   reserved 1;\\n85: \\n86:   reserved \\\"async_mode\\\";\\n87: \\n88:   // Each request message will include one of the following sub-messages. Unless ``observability_mode`` is ``true``, the server must send back a\\n96:     // ``HeaderResponse`` message, an ``ImmediateResponse`` message, or close the stream.\\n97:     HttpHeaders request_headers = 2;\\n98: \\n99:     // Information about the HTTP response headers, as well as peer info and additional\\n100:     // properties. Unless ``observability_mode`` is ``true``, the server must send back a\\n101:     // ``HeaderResponse`` message or close the stream.\\n102:     HttpHeaders response_headers = 3;\\n103: \\n104:     // A chunk of the HTTP request body. syntax = \\\"proto3\\\";\\n2: \\n3: package envoy.service.ext_proc.v3;\\n4: \\n5: import \\\"envoy/config/core/v3/base.proto\\\";\\n6: import \\\"envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3/processing_mode.proto\\\";\\n7: import \\\"envoy/type/v3/http_status.proto\\\";\\n8: \\n9: import \\\"google/protobuf/duration.proto\\\";\\n10: import \\\"google/protobuf/struct.proto\\\";\\n11: \\n12: import \\\"xds/annotations/v3/status.proto\\\";\\n13: \\n14: import \\\"envoy/annotations/deprecation.proto\\\";\\n15: import \\\"udpa/annotations/status.proto\\\";\\n16: import \\\"validate/validate.proto\\\";\\n17: \\n18: option java_package = \\\"io.envoyproxy.envoy.service.ext_proc.v3\\\";\\n19: option java_outer_classname = \\\"ExternalProcessorProto\\\";\\n20: option java_multiple_files = true;\\n21: option go_package = \\\"github.com/envoyproxy/go-control-plane/envoy/service/ext_proc/v3;ext_procv3\\\";\\n22: option (udpa.annotations.file_status).package_version_status = ACTIVE;\\n23: \\n24: // [#protodoc-title: External processing service]\\n25: \\n26: // A service that can access and modify HTTP requests and responses as part of a filter chain.\\n27: // The overall external processing protocol works like this:\\n28: //\\n29: // 1. The data plane sends to the service information about the HTTP request.\\n30: // 2. The service sends back a ``ProcessingResponse`` message that directs the data plane to either\\n31: //    stop processing, continue without it, or send it the next chunk of the message body.\\n32: // 3. If so requested, the data plane sends the server the message body in chunks, or the entire\\n33: //    body at once. In either case, the server may send back a ``ProcessingResponse`` for each\\n34: //    message it receives, or wait for a certain amount of body chunks to be received before\\n35: //    streaming back the ``ProcessingResponse`` messages.\\n36: // 4. If so requested, the data plane sends the server the HTTP trailers, and the server sends back\\n37: //    a ``ProcessingResponse``.\\n38: // 5. At this point, request processing is done, and we pick up again at step 1 when the data plane\\n39: //    receives a response from the upstream server.\\n40: // 6. At any point above, if the server closes the gRPC stream cleanly, then the data plane\\n41: //    proceeds without consulting the server.\\n42: // 7. At any point above, if the server closes the gRPC stream with an error, then the data plane\\n43: //    returns a ``500`` error to the client, unless the filter was configured to ignore errors.\\n44: //\\n45: // In other words, the process is a request/response conversation, but using a gRPC stream to make\\n46: // it easier for the server to maintain state.\\n47: service ExternalProcessor {\\n48:   // This begins the bidirectional stream that the data plane will use to\\n49:   // give the server control over what the filter does. The actual\\n50:   // protocol is described by the ``ProcessingRequest`` and ``ProcessingResponse``\\n51:   // messages below.\\n52:   rpc Process(stream ProcessingRequest) returns (stream ProcessingResponse) {\\n53:   }\\n54: }\\n55: \\n56: // This message specifies the filter protocol configurations which will be sent to the ext_proc\\n57: // server in a :ref:`ProcessingRequest <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingRequest>`.\\n58: // If the server does not support these protocol configurations, it may choose to close the gRPC\\n59: // stream. If the server supports these protocol configurations, it should respond based on the\\n60: // API specifications.\\n61: message ProtocolConfiguration {\\n62:   // Specifies the filter configuration\\n63:   // :ref:`request_body_mode <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingMode.request_body_mode>`.\\n64:   envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingMode.BodySendMode request_body_mode = 1\\n65:       [(validate.rules).enum = {defined_only: true}];\\n66: \\n67:   // Specifies the filter configuration\\n68:   // :ref:`response_body_mode <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingMode.response_body_mode>`.\\n69:   envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingMode.BodySendMode response_body_mode = 2\\n70:       [(validate.rules).enum = {defined_only: true}];\\n71: \\n72:   // Specifies the filter configuration\\n73:   // :ref:`send_body_without_waiting_for_header_response <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.send_body_without_waiting_for_header_response>`.\\n74:   // If the client is waiting for a header response from the server, setting to ``true`` means the\\n75:   // client will send the body to the server as it arrives. Setting to ``false`` means the client\\n76:   // will buffer the arrived data and not send it to the server immediately.\\n77:   bool send_body_without_waiting_for_header_response = 3;\\n78: }\\n79: \\n80: // This represents the different types of messages that the data plane can send\\n81: // to an external processing server.\\n82: // [#next-free-field: 12]\\n83: message ProcessingRequest {\\n84:   reserved 1;\\n85: \\n86:   reserved \\\"async_mode\\\";\\n87: \\n88:   // Each request message will include one of the following sub-messages. Servers may use this to intelligently control how requests\\n225:   // are processed based on the headers and other metadata that they see.\\n226:   //\\n227:   // This field is only applicable when servers are responding to the header requests. import \"validate/validate.proto\";\n17: \n18: option java_package = \"io.envoyproxy.envoy.service.ext_proc.v3\";\n19: option java_outer_classname = \"ExternalProcessorProto\";\n20: option java_multiple_files = true;\n21: option go_package = \"github.com/envoyproxy/go-control-plane/envoy/service/ext_proc/v3;ext_procv3\";\n22: option (udpa.annotations.file_status).package_version_status = ACTIVE;\n23: \n24: // [#protodoc-title: External processing service]\n25: \n26: // A service that can access and modify HTTP requests and responses as part of a filter chain.\n27: // The overall external processing protocol works like this:\n28: //\n29: // 1. The data plane sends to the service information about the HTTP request.\n30: // 2. The service sends back a ``ProcessingResponse`` message that directs the data plane to either\n31: //    stop processing, continue without it, or send it the next chunk of the message body.\n32: // 3. If so requested, the data plane sends the server the message body in chunks, or the entire\n33: //    body at once. In either case, the server may send back a ``ProcessingResponse`` for each\n34: //    message it receives, or wait for a certain amount of body chunks to be received before\n35: //    streaming back the ``ProcessingResponse`` messages.\n36: // 4. If so requested, the data plane sends the server the HTTP trailers, and the server sends back\n37: //    a ``ProcessingResponse``.\n38: // 5. At this point, request processing is done, and we pick up again at step 1 when the data plane\n39: //    receives a response from the upstream server.\n40: // 6. At any point above, if the server closes the gRPC stream cleanly, then the data plane\n41: //    proceeds without consulting the server.\n42: // 7. At any point above, if the server closes the gRPC stream with an error, then the data plane\n43: //    returns a ``500`` error to the client, unless the filter was configured to ignore errors.\n44: //\n45: // In other words, the process is a request/response conversation, but using a gRPC stream to make\n46: // it easier for the server to maintain state.\n47: service ExternalProcessor {\n48:   // This begins the bidirectional stream that the data plane will use to\n49:   // give the server control over what the filter does. The actual\n50:   // protocol is described by the ``ProcessingRequest`` and ``ProcessingResponse``\n51:   // messages below.\n52:   rpc Process(stream ProcessingRequest) returns (stream ProcessingResponse) {\n53:   }\n54: }\n55: \n56: // This message specifies the filter protocol configurations which will be sent to the ext_proc\n57: // server in a :ref:`ProcessingRequest <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingRequest>`.\n58: // If the server does not support these protocol configurations, it may choose to close the gRPC\n59: // stream. If the server supports these protocol configurations, it should respond based on the\n60: // API specifications.\n61: message ProtocolConfiguration {\n62:   // Specifies the filter configuration\n63:   // :ref:`request_body_mode <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingMode.request_body_mode>`.\n64:   envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingMode.BodySendMode request_body_mode = 1\n65:       [(validate.rules).enum = {defined_only: true}];\n66: \n67:   // Specifies the filter configuration\n68:   // :ref:`response_body_mode <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingMode.response_body_mode>`.\n69:   envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingMode.BodySendMode response_body_mode = 2\n70:       [(validate.rules).enum = {defined_only: true}];\n71: \n72:   // Specifies the filter configuration\n73:   // :ref:`send_body_without_waiting_for_header_response <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.send_body_without_waiting_for_header_response>`.\n74:   // If the client is waiting for a header response from the server, setting to ``true`` means the\n75:   // client will send the body to the server as it arrives. Setting to ``false`` means the client\n76:   // will buffer the arrived data and not send it to the server immediately.\n77:   bool send_body_without_waiting_for_header_response = 3;\n78: }\n79: \n80: // This represents the different types of messages that the data plane can send\n81: // to an external processing server.\n82: // [#next-free-field: 12]\n83: message ProcessingRequest {\n84:   reserved 1;\n85: \n86:   reserved \"async_mode\";\n87: \n88:   // Each request message will include one of the following sub-messages. Which\n89:   // ones are set for a particular HTTP request/response depend on the\n90:   // processing mode.\n91:   oneof request {\n92:     option (validate.required) = true;\n93: \n94:     // Information about the HTTP request headers, as well as peer info and additional\n95:     // properties. Unless ``observability_mode`` is ``true``, the server must send back a\n96:     // ``HeaderResponse`` message, an ``ImmediateResponse`` message, or close the stream.\n97:     HttpHeaders request_headers = 2;\n98: \n99:     // Information about the HTTP response headers, as well as peer info and additional\n100:     // properties. Unless ``observability_mode`` is ``true``, the server must send back a\n101:     // ``HeaderResponse`` message or close the stream.\n102:     HttpHeaders response_headers = 3;\n103: \n104:     // A chunk of the HTTP request body. Unless ``observability_mode`` is ``true``, the server must\n105:     // send back a ``BodyResponse`` message, an ``ImmediateResponse`` message, or close the stream.\n106:     HttpBody request_body = 4;\n107: \n108:     // A chunk of the HTTP response body. ProtocolConfiguration protocol_config = 11;\n151: }\n152: \n153: // This represents the different types of messages the server may send back to the data plane\n154: // when the ``observability_mode`` to create a locally generated response, send it\n193:     // downstream, and stop processing additional filters and ignore any\n194:     // additional messages received from the remote server for this request or\n195:     // response. If a response has already started -- for example, if this\n196:     // message is sent response to a ``response_body`` message -- then\n197:     // this will either ship the reply directly to the downstream codec,\n198:     // or reset the stream.\n199:     ImmediateResponse immediate_response = 7;\n200: \n201:     // The server sends back this message to initiate or continue local response streaming.\n202:     // The server must initiate local response streaming with the ``headers_response`` in response\n203:     // to a ``ProcessingRequest`` with the ``request_headers`` only.\n204:     // The server may follow up with multiple messages containing ``body_response``. The server must\n205:     // indicate end of stream by setting ``end_of_stream`` to ``true`` in the ``headers_response``\n206:     // or ``body_response`` message or by sending a ``trailers_response`` message.\n207:     // The client may send a ``request_body`` or ``request_trailers`` to the server depending on\n208:     // configuration.\n209:     // The streaming local response can only be sent when the ``request_header_mode`` in the filter\n210:     // :ref:`processing_mode <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.processing_mode>`\n211:     // is set to ``SEND``. This metadata will be placed in the namespace(s) specified by the top-level\n220:   // field name(s) of the struct.\n221:   google.protobuf.Struct dynamic_metadata = 8;\n222: \n223:   // Override how parts of the HTTP request and response are processed for the duration of this\n224:   // particular request/response only. Servers may use this to intelligently control how requests\n225:   // are processed based on the headers and other metadata that they see.\n226:   //\n227:   // This field is only applicable when servers are responding to the header requests. If it is set\n228:   // in the response to the body or trailer requests, it will be ignored by the data plane.\n229:   // It is also ignored by the data plane when the ext_proc filter config\n230:   // :ref:`allow_mode_override <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.allow_mode_override>`\n231:   // is set to ``false``, or\n232:   // :ref:`send_body_without_waiting_for_header_response <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.send_body_without_waiting_for_header_response>`\n233:   // is set to ``true``.\n234:   envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingMode mode_override = 9;\n235: \n236:   // [#not-implemented-hide:]\n237:   // Used only in ``FULL_DUPLEX_STREAMED`` and ``GRPC`` body send modes.\n238:   // Instructs the data plane to stop sending body data and to send a\n239:   // half-close on the ext_proc stream. The ext_proc server should then echo\n240:   // back all subsequent body contents as-is until it sees the client's\n241:   // half-close, at which point the ext_proc server can terminate the stream\n242:   // with an OK status. This provides a safe way for the ext_proc server\n243:   // to indicate that it does not need to see the rest of the stream;\n244:   // without this, the ext_proc server could not terminate the stream\n245:   // early, because it would wind up dropping any body contents that the\n246:   // client had already sent before it saw the ext_proc stream termination.\n247:   bool request_drain = 12;\n248: \n249:   // When the ext_proc server receives a request message and needs more time to process it, it\n250:   // sends back a ``ProcessingResponse`` message with a new timeout value. When the data plane\n251:   // receives this response message, it ignores other fields in the response, stops the original\n252:   // timer (which has the timeout value specified in\n253:   // :ref:`message_timeout <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.message_timeout>`),\n254:   // and starts a new timer with this ``override_message_timeout`` value while keeping the data\n255:   // plane ext_proc filter state machine intact.\n256:   //\n257:   // The value must be >= 1ms and <=\n258:   // :ref:`max_message_timeout <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.max_message_timeout>`.\n259:   // Such a message can be sent at most once in a particular data plane ext_proc filter processing\n260:   // state. Upon connecting, the management server can send a\\n23: // :ref:`LoadStatsResponse <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.load_stats.v3.LoadStatsResponse>` to a node it is\\n24: // interested in getting the load reports for. Envoy in this node will start sending\\n25: // :ref:`LoadStatsRequest <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.load_stats.v3.LoadStatsRequest>`. For receiving LB assignments, the steps are:\\n32:   // 1, The management server is configured with per cluster/zone/load metric\\n33:   //    capacity configuration. The capacity configuration definition is\\n34:   //    outside of the scope of this document.\\n35:   // 2. Envoy issues a standard {Stream,Fetch}Endpoints request for the clusters\\n36:   //    to balance.\\n37:   //\\n38:   // Independently, Envoy will initiate a StreamLoadStats bidi stream with a\\n39:   // management server:\\n40:   // 1. Once a connection establishes, the management server publishes a\\n41:   //    LoadStatsResponse for all clusters it is interested in learning load\\n42:   //    stats about.\\n43:   // 2. For each cluster, Envoy load balances incoming traffic to upstream hosts\\n44:   //    based on per-zone weights and/or per-instance weights (if specified)\\n45:   //    based on intra-zone LbPolicy. This information comes from the above\\n46:   //    {Stream,Fetch}Endpoints.\\n47:   // 3. When upstream hosts reply, they optionally add header <define header\\n48:   //    name> with ASCII representation of EndpointLoadMetricStats.\\n49:   // 4. Envoy aggregates load reports over the period of time given to it in\\n50:   //    LoadStatsResponse.load_reporting_interval. This includes aggregation\\n51:   //    stats Envoy maintains by itself (total_requests, rpc_errors etc.) as\\n52:   //    well as load metrics from upstream hosts.\\n53:   // 5. When the timer of load_reporting_interval expires, Envoy sends new\\n54:   //    LoadStatsRequest filled with load reports for each cluster.\\n55:   // 6. The management server uses the load reports from all reported Envoys\\n56:   //    from around the world, computes global assignment and prepares traffic\\n57:   //    assignment destined for each zone Envoys are located in. This is only a minimum for two reasons:\\n90:   //\\n91:   // 1. There may be some delay from when the timer fires until stats sampling occurs.\\n92:   // 2. For clusters that were already feature in the previous ``LoadStatsResponse``, any traffic\\n93:   //    that is observed in between the corresponding previous ``LoadStatsRequest`` and this\\n94:   //    ``LoadStatsResponse`` will also be accumulated and billed to the cluster. This avoids a period\\n95:   //    of inobservability that might otherwise exists between the messages. New clusters are not\\n96:   //    subject to this consideration.\\n97:   google.protobuf.Duration load_reporting_interval = 2;\\n98: \\n99:   // Set to ``true`` if the management server supports endpoint granularity\\n100:   // report.\\n101:   bool report_endpoint_granularity = 3;\\n102: }\\n103: \",\"url\":\"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/data-plane-api--84e84367@d9596a37e1620efc399ac5ce4821e268985e7dcc/-/blob/envoy/service/load_stats/v3/lrs.proto\"}"}]},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"db0ec1da-ccdb-4974-834b-3a57c048888e","uuid":"583e11f2-5666-4ccd-9d5e-11bac2bcd8ab","tool_use_result":{"content":"{\"content\":\"1: syntax = \\\"proto3\\\";\\n2: \\n3: package envoy.service.load_stats.v3;\\n4: \\n5: import \\\"envoy/config/core/v3/base.proto\\\";\\n6: import \\\"envoy/config/endpoint/v3/load_report.proto\\\";\\n7: \\n8: import \\\"google/protobuf/duration.proto\\\";\\n9: \\n10: import \\\"udpa/annotations/status.proto\\\";\\n11: import \\\"udpa/annotations/versioning.proto\\\";\\n12: \\n13: option java_package = \\\"io.envoyproxy.envoy.service.load_stats.v3\\\";\\n14: option java_outer_classname = \\\"LrsProto\\\";\\n15: option java_multiple_files = true;\\n16: option go_package = \\\"github.com/envoyproxy/go-control-plane/envoy/service/load_stats/v3;load_statsv3\\\";\\n17: option (udpa.annotations.file_status).package_version_status = ACTIVE;\\n18: \\n19: // [#protodoc-title: Load reporting service (LRS)]\\n20: \\n21: // Load Reporting Service is an Envoy API to emit load reports. Envoy aggregates load reports over the period of time given to it in\n50:   //    LoadStatsResponse.load_reporting_interval. This includes aggregation\n51:   //    stats Envoy maintains by itself (total_requests, rpc_errors etc.) as\n52:   //    well as load metrics from upstream hosts.\n53:   // 5. When the timer of load_reporting_interval expires, Envoy sends new\n54:   //    LoadStatsRequest filled with load reports for each cluster.\n55:   // 6. The management server uses the load reports from all reported Envoys\n56:   //    from around the world, computes global assignment and prepares traffic\n57:   //    assignment destined for each zone Envoys are located in. Goto 2.\n58:   rpc StreamLoadStats(stream LoadStatsRequest) returns (stream LoadStatsResponse) {\n59:   }\n60: }\n61: \n62: // A load report Envoy sends to the management server.\n63: message LoadStatsRequest {\n64:   option (udpa.annotations.versioning).previous_message_type =\n65:       \"envoy.service.load_stats.v2.LoadStatsRequest\";\n66: \n67:   // Node identifier for Envoy instance.\n68:   config.core.v3.Node node = 1;\n69: \n70:   // A list of load stats to report.\n71:   repeated config.endpoint.v3.ClusterStats cluster_stats = 2;\n72: }\n73: \n74: // The management server sends envoy a LoadStatsResponse with all clusters it\n75: // is interested in learning load stats about.\n76: message LoadStatsResponse {\n77:   option (udpa.annotations.versioning).previous_message_type =\n78:       \"envoy.service.load_stats.v2.LoadStatsResponse\";\n79: \n80:   // Clusters to report stats for.\n81:   // Not populated if ``send_all_clusters`` is true.\n82:   repeated string clusters = 1;\n83: \n84:   // If true, the client should send all clusters it knows about.\n85:   // Only clients that advertise the \"envoy.lrs.supports_send_all_clusters\" capability in their\n86:   // :ref:`client_features<envoy_v3_api_field_config.core.v3.Node.client_features>` field will honor this field.\n87:   bool send_all_clusters = 4;\n88: \n89:   // The minimum interval of time to collect stats over. This is only a minimum for two reasons:\n90:   //\n91:   // 1. There may be some delay from when the timer fires until stats sampling occurs.\n92:   // 2. For clusters that were already feature in the previous ``LoadStatsResponse``, any traffic\n93:   //    that is observed in between the corresponding previous ``LoadStatsRequest`` and this\n94:   //    ``LoadStatsResponse`` will also be accumulated and billed to the cluster. This avoids a period\n95:   //    of inobservability that might otherwise exists between the messages. New clusters are not\n96:   //    subject to this consideration.\n97:   google.protobuf.Duration load_reporting_interval = 2;\n98: \n99:   // Set to ``true`` if the management server supports endpoint granularity\n100:   // report.\n101:   bool report_endpoint_granularity = 3;\n102: }\n103: ","url":"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/data-plane-api--84e84367@d9596a37e1620efc399ac5ce4821e268985e7dcc/-/blob/envoy/service/load_stats/v3/lrs.proto"}}}

{"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_018vk7oSBaJ2YjkipdpoJdrG","type":"tool_result","content":"{\"content\":\"1: syntax = \\\"proto3\\\";\\n2: \\n3: package envoy.service.rate_limit_quota.v3;\\n4: \\n5: import \\\"envoy/type/v3/ratelimit_strategy.proto\\\";\\n6: \\n7: import \\\"google/protobuf/duration.proto\\\";\\n8: \\n9: import \\\"xds/annotations/v3/status.proto\\\";\\n10: \\n11: import \\\"udpa/annotations/status.proto\\\";\\n12: import \\\"validate/validate.proto\\\";\\n13: \\n14: option java_package = \\\"io.envoyproxy.envoy.service.rate_limit_quota.v3\\\";\\n15: option java_outer_classname = \\\"RlqsProto\\\";\\n16: option java_multiple_files = true;\\n17: option go_package = \\\"github.com/envoyproxy/go-control-plane/envoy/service/rate_limit_quota/v3;rate_limit_quotav3\\\";\\n18: option (udpa.annotations.file_status).package_version_status = ACTIVE;\\n19: option (xds.annotations.v3.file_status).work_in_progress = true;\\n20: \\n21: // [#protodoc-title: Rate Limit Quota Service (RLQS)]\\n22: \\n23: // The Rate Limit Quota Service (RLQS) is a Envoy global rate limiting service that allows to\\n24: // delegate rate limit decisions to a remote service. The service will aggregate the usage reports\\n25: // from multiple data plane instances, and distribute Rate Limit Assignments to each instance\\n26: // based on its business logic. The logic is outside of the scope of the protocol API.\\n27: //\\n28: // The protocol is designed as a streaming-first API. It utilizes watch-like subscription model.\\n29: // The data plane groups requests into Quota Buckets as directed by the filter config,\\n30: // and periodically reports them to the RLQS server along with the Bucket identifier, :ref:`BucketId\\n31: // <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.rate_limit_quota.v3.BucketId>`. Once RLQS server has collected enough\\n32: // reports to make a decision, it'll send back the assignment with the rate limiting instructions.\\n33: //\\n34: // The first report sent by the data plane is interpreted by the RLQS server as a \\\"watch\\\" request,\\n35: // indicating that the data plane instance is interested in receiving further updates for the\\n36: // ``BucketId``. From then on, RLQS server may push assignments to this instance at will, even if\\n37: // the instance is not sending usage reports. It's the responsibility of the RLQS server\\n38: // to determine when the data plane instance didn't send ``BucketId`` reports for too long,\\n39: // and to respond with the :ref:`AbandonAction\\n40: // <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.rate_limit_quota.v3.RateLimitQuotaResponse.BucketAction.AbandonAction>`,\\n41: // indicating that the server has now stopped sending quota assignments for the ``BucketId`` bucket,\\n42: // and the data plane instance should :ref:`abandon\\n43: // <envoy_v3_api_field_service.rate_limit_quota.v3.RateLimitQuotaResponse.BucketAction.abandon_action>`\\n44: // it.\\n45: //\\n46: // If for any reason the RLQS client doesn't receive the initial assignment for the reported bucket,\\n47: // in order to prevent memory exhaustion, the data plane will limit the time such bucket\\n48: // is retained. The exact time to wait for the initial assignment is chosen by the filter,\\n49: // and may vary based on the implementation.\\n50: // Once the duration ends, the data plane will stop reporting bucket usage, reject any enqueued\\n51: // requests, and purge the bucket from the memory. Subsequent requests matched into the bucket\\n52: // will re-initialize the bucket in the \\\"no assignment\\\" state, restarting the reports.\\n53: //\\n54: // Refer to Rate Limit Quota :ref:`configuration overview <config_http_filters_rate_limit_quota>`\\n55: // for further details.\\n56: \\n57: // Defines the Rate Limit Quota Service (RLQS).\\n58: service RateLimitQuotaService {\\n59:   // Main communication channel: the data plane sends usage reports to the RLQS server,\\n60:   // and the server asynchronously responding with the assignments.\\n61:   rpc StreamRateLimitQuotas(stream RateLimitQuotaUsageReports)\\n62:       returns (stream RateLimitQuotaResponse) {\\n63:   }\\n64: }\\n65: \\n66: message RateLimitQuotaUsageReports {\\n67:   // The usage report for a bucket.\\n68:   //\\n69:   // .. note::\\n70:   //   Note that the first report sent for a ``BucketId`` indicates to the RLQS server that\\n71:   //   the RLQS client is subscribing for the future assignments for this ``BucketId``.\\n72:   message BucketQuotaUsage {\\n73:     // ``BucketId`` for which request quota usage is reported.\\n74:     BucketId bucket_id = 1 [(validate.rules).message = {required: true}];\\n75: \\n76:     // Time elapsed since the last report.\\n77:     google.protobuf.Duration time_elapsed = 2 [(validate.rules).duration = {\\n78:       required: true\\n79:       gt {}\\n80:     }];\\n81: \\n82:     // Requests the data plane has allowed through.\\n83:     uint64 num_requests_allowed = 3;\\n84: \\n85:     // Requests throttled.\\n86:     uint64 num_requests_denied = 4;\\n87:   }\\n88: \\n89:   // All quota requests must specify the domain. This enables sharing the quota\\n90:   // server between different applications without fear of overlap.\\n91:   // E.g., \\\"envoy\\\".\\n92:   //\\n93:   // Should only be provided in the first report, all subsequent messages on the same\\n94:   // stream are considered to be in the same domain. In case the domain needs to be\\n95:   // changes, close the stream, and reopen a new one with the different domain.\\n96:   string domain = 1 [(validate.rules).string = {min_len: 1}];\\n97: \\n98:   // A list of quota usage reports. The list is processed by the RLQS server in the same order\\n99:   // it's provided by the client.\\n100:   repeated BucketQuotaUsage bucket_quota_usages = 2 [(validate.rules).repeated = {min_items: 1}];\\n101: }\\n102: \\n103: message RateLimitQuotaResponse {\\n104:   // Commands the data plane to apply one of the actions to the bucket with the\\n105:   // :ref:`bucket_id <envoy_v3_api_field_service.rate_limit_quota.v3.RateLimitQuotaResponse.BucketAction.bucket_id>`.\\n106:   message BucketAction {\\n107:     // Quota assignment for the bucket. Configures the rate limiting strategy and the duration\\n108:     // for the given :ref:`bucket_id\\n109:     // <envoy_v3_api_field_service.rate_limit_quota.v3.RateLimitQuotaResponse.BucketAction.bucket_id>`.\\n110:     //\\n111:     // **Applying the first assignment to the bucket**\\n112:     //\\n113:     // Once the data plane receives the ``QuotaAssignmentAction``, it must send the current usage\\n114:     // report for the bucket, and start rate limiting requests matched into the bucket\\n115:     // using the strategy configured in the :ref:`rate_limit_strategy\\n116:     // <envoy_v3_api_field_service.rate_limit_quota.v3.RateLimitQuotaResponse.BucketAction.QuotaAssignmentAction.rate_limit_strategy>`\\n117:     // field. The assignment becomes bucket's ``active`` assignment.\\n118:     //\\n119:     // **Expiring the assignment**\\n120:     //\\n121:     // The duration of the assignment defined in the :ref:`assignment_time_to_live\\n122:     // <envoy_v3_api_field_service.rate_limit_quota.v3.RateLimitQuotaResponse.BucketAction.QuotaAssignmentAction.assignment_time_to_live>`\\n123:     // field. When the duration runs off, the assignment is ``expired``, and no longer ``active``.\\n124:     // The data plane should stop applying the rate limiting strategy to the bucket, and transition\\n125:     // the bucket to the \\\"expired assignment\\\" state. This activates the behavior configured in the\\n126:     // :ref:`expired_assignment_behavior <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.rate_limit_quota.v3.RateLimitQuotaBucketSettings.expired_assignment_behavior>`\\n127:     // field.\\n128:     //\\n129:     // **Replacing the assignment**\\n130:     //\\n131:     // * If the rate limiting strategy is different from bucket's ``active`` assignment, or\\n132:     //   the current bucket assignment is ``expired``, the data plane must immediately\\n133:     //   end the current assignment, report the bucket usage, and apply the new assignment.\\n134:     //   The new assignment becomes bucket's ``active`` assignment.\\n135:     // * If the rate limiting strategy is the same as the bucket's ``active`` (not ``expired``)\\n136:     //   assignment, the data plane should extend the duration of the ``active`` assignment\\n137:     //   for the duration of the new assignment provided in the :ref:`assignment_time_to_live\\n138:     //   <envoy_v3_api_field_service.rate_limit_quota.v3.RateLimitQuotaResponse.BucketAction.QuotaAssignmentAction.assignment_time_to_live>`\\n139:     //   field. The ``active`` assignment is considered unchanged.\\n140:     message QuotaAssignmentAction {\\n141:       // A duration after which the assignment is be considered ``expired``. The process of the\\n142:       // expiration is described :ref:`above\\n143:       // <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.rate_limit_quota.v3.RateLimitQuotaResponse.BucketAction.QuotaAssignmentAction>`.\\n144:       //\\n145:       // * If unset, the assignment has no expiration date.\\n146:       // * If set to ``0``, the assignment expires immediately, forcing the client into the\\n147:       //   :ref:`\\\"expired assignment\\\"\\n148:       //   <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.rate_limit_quota.v3.RateLimitQuotaBucketSettings.ExpiredAssignmentBehavior.expired_assignment_behavior_timeout>`\\n149:       //   state. This may be used by the RLQS server in cases when it needs clients to proactively\\n150:       //   fall back to the pre-configured :ref:`ExpiredAssignmentBehavior\\n151:       //   <envoy_v3_api_msg_extensions.filters.http.rate_limit_quota.v3.RateLimitQuotaBucketSettings.ExpiredAssignmentBehavior>`,\\n152:       //   f.e. before the server going into restart.\\n153:       //\\n154:       // .. attention::\\n155:       //   Note that :ref:`expiring\\n156:       //   <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.rate_limit_quota.v3.RateLimitQuotaResponse.BucketAction.QuotaAssignmentAction>`\\n157:       //   the assignment is not the same as :ref:`abandoning\\n158:       //   <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.rate_limit_quota.v3.RateLimitQuotaResponse.BucketAction.AbandonAction>`\\n159:       //   the assignment. While expiring the assignment just transitions the bucket to\\n160:       //   the \\\"expired assignment\\\" state; abandoning the assignment completely erases\\n161:       //   the bucket from the data plane memory, and stops the usage reports.\\n162:       google.protobuf.Duration assignment_time_to_live = 2 [(validate.rules).duration = {gte {}}];\\n163: \\n164:       // Configures the local rate limiter for the request matched to the bucket.\\n165:       // If not set, allow all requests.\\n166:       type.v3.RateLimitStrategy rate_limit_strategy = 3;\\n167:     }\\n168: \\n169:     // Abandon action for the bucket. Indicates that the RLQS server will no longer be\\n170:     // sending updates for the given :ref:`bucket_id\\n171:     // <envoy_v3_api_field_service.rate_limit_quota.v3.RateLimitQuotaResponse.BucketAction.bucket_id>`.\\n172:     //\\n173:     // If no requests are reported for a bucket, after some time the server considers the bucket\\n174:     // inactive. The server stops tracking the bucket, and instructs the the data plane to abandon\\n175:     // the bucket via this message.\\n176:     //\\n177:     // **Abandoning the assignment**\\n178:     //\\n179:     // The data plane is to erase the bucket (including its usage data) from the memory.\\n180:     // It should stop tracking the bucket, and stop reporting its usage. This effectively resets\\n181:     // the data plane to the state prior to matching the first request into the bucket.\\n182:     //\\n183:     // **Restarting the subscription**\\n184:     //\\n185:     // If a new request is matched into a bucket previously abandoned, the data plane must behave\\n186:     // as if it has never tracked the bucket, and it's the first request matched into it:\\n187:     //\\n188:     // 1. The process of :ref:`subscription and reporting\\n189:     //    <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.rate_limit_quota.v3.RateLimitQuotaBucketSettings.reporting_interval>`\\n190:     //    starts from the beginning.\\n191:     //\\n192:     // 2. The bucket transitions to the :ref:`\\\"no assignment\\\"\\n193:     //    <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.rate_limit_quota.v3.RateLimitQuotaBucketSettings.no_assignment_behavior>`\\n194:     //    state.\\n195:     //\\n196:     // 3. Once the new assignment is received, it's applied per\\n197:     //    \\\"Applying the first assignment to the bucket\\\" section of the :ref:`QuotaAssignmentAction\\n198:     //    <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.rate_limit_quota.v3.RateLimitQuotaResponse.BucketAction.QuotaAssignmentAction>`.\\n199:     message AbandonAction {\\n200:     }\\n201: \\n202:     // ``BucketId`` for which request the action is applied.\\n203:     BucketId bucket_id = 1 [(validate.rules).message = {required: true}];\\n204: \\n205:     oneof bucket_action {\\n206:       option (validate.required) = true;\\n207: \\n208:       // Apply the quota assignment to the bucket.\\n209:       //\\n210:       // Commands the data plane to apply a rate limiting strategy to the bucket.\\n211:       // The process of applying and expiring the rate limiting strategy is detailed in the\\n212:       // :ref:`QuotaAssignmentAction\\n213:       // <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.rate_limit_quota.v3.RateLimitQuotaResponse.BucketAction.QuotaAssignmentAction>`\\n214:       // message.\\n215:       QuotaAssignmentAction quota_assignment_action = 2;\\n216: \\n217:       // Abandon the bucket.\\n218:       //\\n219:       // Commands the data plane to abandon the bucket.\\n220:       // The process of abandoning the bucket is described in the :ref:`AbandonAction\\n221:       // <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.rate_limit_quota.v3.RateLimitQuotaResponse.BucketAction.AbandonAction>`\\n222:       // message.\\n223:       AbandonAction abandon_action = 3;\\n224:     }\\n225:   }\\n226: \\n227:   // An ordered list of actions to be applied to the buckets. The actions are applied in the\\n228:   // given order, from top to bottom.\\n229:   repeated BucketAction bucket_action = 1 [(validate.rules).repeated = {min_items: 1}];\\n230: }\\n231: \\n232: // The identifier for the bucket. Used to match the bucket between the control plane (RLQS server),\\n233: // and the data plane (RLQS client), f.e.:\\n234: //\\n235: // * the data plane sends a usage report for requests matched into the bucket with ``BucketId``\\n236: //   to the control plane\\n237: // * the control plane sends an assignment for the bucket with ``BucketId`` to the data plane\\n238: //   Bucket ID.\\n239: //\\n240: // Example:\\n241: //\\n242: // .. validated-code-block:: yaml\\n243: //   :type-name: envoy.service.rate_limit_quota.v3.BucketId\\n244: //\\n245: //   bucket:\\n246: //     name: my_bucket\\n247: //     env: staging\\n248: //\\n249: // .. note::\\n250: //   The order of ``BucketId`` keys do not matter. The service will aggregate the usage reports\\n25: // from multiple data plane instances, and distribute Rate Limit Assignments to each instance\\n26: // based on its business logic. The logic is outside of the scope of the protocol API.\\n27: //\\n28: // The protocol is designed as a streaming-first API. It utilizes watch-like subscription model.\\n29: // The data plane groups requests into Quota Buckets as directed by the filter config,\\n30: // and periodically reports them to the RLQS server along with the Bucket identifier, :ref:`BucketId\\n31: // <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.rate_limit_quota.v3.BucketId>`. Once RLQS server has collected enough\\n32: // reports to make a decision, it'll send back the assignment with the rate limiting instructions.\\n33: //\\n34: // The first report sent by the data plane is interpreted by the RLQS server as a \\\"watch\\\" request,\\n35: // indicating that the data plane instance is interested in receiving further updates for the\\n36: // ``BucketId``. From then on, RLQS server may push assignments to this instance at will, even if\\n37: // the instance is not sending usage reports. It's the responsibility of the RLQS server\\n38: // to determine when the data plane instance didn't send ``BucketId`` reports for too long,\\n39: // and to respond with the :ref:`AbandonAction\\n40: // <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.rate_limit_quota.v3.RateLimitQuotaResponse.BucketAction.AbandonAction>`,\\n41: // indicating that the server has now stopped sending quota assignments for the ``BucketId`` bucket,\\n42: // and the data plane instance should :ref:`abandon\\n43: // <envoy_v3_api_field_service.rate_limit_quota.v3.RateLimitQuotaResponse.BucketAction.abandon_action>`\\n44: // it.\\n45: //\\n46: // If for any reason the RLQS client doesn't receive the initial assignment for the reported bucket,\\n47: // in order to prevent memory exhaustion, the data plane will limit the time such bucket\\n48: // is retained. The exact time to wait for the initial assignment is chosen by the filter,\\n49: // and may vary based on the implementation.\\n50: // Once the duration ends, the data plane will stop reporting bucket usage, reject any enqueued\\n51: // requests, and purge the bucket from the memory. Subsequent requests matched into the bucket\\n52: // will re-initialize the bucket in the \\\"no assignment\\\" state, restarting the reports.\\n53: //\\n54: // Refer to Rate Limit Quota :ref:`configuration overview <config_http_filters_rate_limit_quota>`\\n55: // for further details.\\n56: \\n57: // Defines the Rate Limit Quota Service (RLQS).\\n58: service RateLimitQuotaService {\\n59:   // Main communication channel: the data plane sends usage reports to the RLQS server,\\n60:   // and the server asynchronously responding with the assignments.\\n61:   rpc StreamRateLimitQuotas(stream RateLimitQuotaUsageReports)\\n62:       returns (stream RateLimitQuotaResponse) {\\n63:   }\\n64: }\\n65: \\n66: message RateLimitQuotaUsageReports {\\n67:   // The usage report for a bucket.\\n68:   //\\n69:   // .. note::\\n70:   //   Note that the first report sent for a ``BucketId`` indicates to the RLQS server that\\n71:   //   the RLQS client is subscribing for the future assignments for this ``BucketId``.\\n72:   message BucketQuotaUsage {\\n73:     // ``BucketId`` for which request quota usage is reported.\\n74:     BucketId bucket_id = 1 [(validate.rules).message = {required: true}];\\n75: \\n76:     // Time elapsed since the last report.\\n77:     google.protobuf.Duration time_elapsed = 2 [(validate.rules).duration = {\\n78:       required: true\\n79:       gt {}\\n80:     }];\\n81: \\n82:     // Requests the data plane has allowed through.\\n83:     uint64 num_requests_allowed = 3;\\n84: \\n85:     // Requests throttled.\\n86:     uint64 num_requests_denied = 4;\\n87:   }\\n88: \\n89:   // All quota requests must specify the domain. This enables sharing the quota\\n90:   // server between different applications without fear of overlap.\\n91:   // E.g., \\\"envoy\\\".\\n92:   //\\n93:   // Should only be provided in the first report, all subsequent messages on the same\\n94:   // stream are considered to be in the same domain. In case the domain needs to be\\n95:   // changes, close the stream, and reopen a new one with the different domain.\\n96:   string domain = 1 [(validate.rules).string = {min_len: 1}];\\n97: \\n98:   // A list of quota usage reports. The list is processed by the RLQS server in the same order\\n99:   // it's provided by the client.\\n100:   repeated BucketQuotaUsage bucket_quota_usages = 2 [(validate.rules).repeated = {min_items: 1}];\\n101: }\\n102: \\n103: message RateLimitQuotaResponse {\\n104:   // Commands the data plane to apply one of the actions to the bucket with the\\n105:   // :ref:`bucket_id <envoy_v3_api_field_service.rate_limit_quota.v3.RateLimitQuotaResponse.BucketAction.bucket_id>`.\\n106:   message BucketAction {\\n107:     // Quota assignment for the bucket. Configures the rate limiting strategy and the duration\\n108:     // for the given :ref:`bucket_id\\n109:     // <envoy_v3_api_field_service.rate_limit_quota.v3.RateLimitQuotaResponse.BucketAction.bucket_id>`.\\n110:     //\\n111:     // **Applying the first assignment to the bucket**\\n112:     //\\n113:     // Once the data plane receives the ``QuotaAssignmentAction``, it must send the current usage\\n114:     // report for the bucket, and start rate limiting requests matched into the bucket\\n115:     // using the strategy configured in the :ref:`rate_limit_strategy\\n116:     // <envoy_v3_api_field_service.rate_limit_quota.v3.RateLimitQuotaResponse.BucketAction.QuotaAssignmentAction.rate_limit_strategy>`\\n117:     // field. The assignment becomes bucket's ``active`` assignment.\\n118:     //\\n119:     // **Expiring the assignment**\\n120:     //\\n121:     // The duration of the assignment defined in the :ref:`assignment_time_to_live\\n122:     // <envoy_v3_api_field_service.rate_limit_quota.v3.RateLimitQuotaResponse.BucketAction.QuotaAssignmentAction.assignment_time_to_live>`\\n123:     // field. When the duration runs off, the assignment is ``expired``, and no longer ``active``.\\n124:     // The data plane should stop applying the rate limiting strategy to the bucket, and transition\\n125:     // the bucket to the \\\"expired assignment\\\" state. This activates the behavior configured in the\\n126:     // :ref:`expired_assignment_behavior <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.rate_limit_quota.v3.RateLimitQuotaBucketSettings.expired_assignment_behavior>`\\n127:     // field.\\n128:     //\\n129:     // **Replacing the assignment**\\n130:     //\\n131:     // * If the rate limiting strategy is different from bucket's ``active`` assignment, or\\n132:     //   the current bucket assignment is ``expired``, the data plane must immediately\\n133:     //   end the current assignment, report the bucket usage, and apply the new assignment.\\n134:     //   The new assignment becomes bucket's ``active`` assignment.\\n135:     // * If the rate limiting strategy is the same as the bucket's ``active`` (not ``expired``)\\n136:     //   assignment, the data plane should extend the duration of the ``active`` assignment\\n137:     //   for the duration of the new assignment provided in the :ref:`assignment_time_to_live\\n138:     //   <envoy_v3_api_field_service.rate_limit_quota.v3.RateLimitQuotaResponse.BucketAction.QuotaAssignmentAction.assignment_time_to_live>`\\n139:     //   field. The ``active`` assignment is considered unchanged.\\n140:     message QuotaAssignmentAction {\\n141:       // A duration after which the assignment is be considered ``expired``. The process of the\\n142:       // expiration is described :ref:`above\\n143:       // <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.rate_limit_quota.v3.RateLimitQuotaResponse.BucketAction.QuotaAssignmentAction>`.\\n144:       //\\n145:       // * If unset, the assignment has no expiration date.\\n146:       // * If set to ``0``, the assignment expires immediately, forcing the client into the\\n147:       //   :ref:`\\\"expired assignment\\\"\\n148:       //   <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.rate_limit_quota.v3.RateLimitQuotaBucketSettings.ExpiredAssignmentBehavior.expired_assignment_behavior_timeout>`\\n149:       //   state. This may be used by the RLQS server in cases when it needs clients to proactively\\n150:       //   fall back to the pre-configured :ref:`ExpiredAssignmentBehavior\\n151:       //   <envoy_v3_api_msg_extensions.filters.http.rate_limit_quota.v3.RateLimitQuotaBucketSettings.ExpiredAssignmentBehavior>`,\\n152:       //   f.e. before the server going into restart.\\n153:       //\\n154:       // .. attention::\\n155:       //   Note that :ref:`expiring\\n156:       //   <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.rate_limit_quota.v3.RateLimitQuotaResponse.BucketAction.QuotaAssignmentAction>`\\n157:       //   the assignment is not the same as :ref:`abandoning\\n158:       //   <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.rate_limit_quota.v3.RateLimitQuotaResponse.BucketAction.AbandonAction>`\\n159:       //   the assignment. While expiring the assignment just transitions the bucket to\\n160:       //   the \\\"expired assignment\\\" state; abandoning the assignment completely erases\\n161:       //   the bucket from the data plane memory, and stops the usage reports.\\n162:       google.protobuf.Duration assignment_time_to_live = 2 [(validate.rules).duration = {gte {}}];\\n163: \\n164:       // Configures the local rate limiter for the request matched to the bucket.\\n165:       // If not set, allow all requests.\\n166:       type.v3.RateLimitStrategy rate_limit_strategy = 3;\\n167:     }\\n168: \\n169:     // Abandon action for the bucket. Indicates that the RLQS server will no longer be\\n170:     // sending updates for the given :ref:`bucket_id\\n171:     // <envoy_v3_api_field_service.rate_limit_quota.v3.RateLimitQuotaResponse.BucketAction.bucket_id>`.\\n172:     //\\n173:     // If no requests are reported for a bucket, after some time the server considers the bucket\\n174:     // inactive. The server stops tracking the bucket, and instructs the the data plane to abandon\\n175:     // the bucket via this message.\\n176:     //\\n177:     // **Abandoning the assignment**\\n178:     //\\n179:     // The data plane is to erase the bucket (including its usage data) from the memory.\\n180:     // It should stop tracking the bucket, and stop reporting its usage. This effectively resets\\n181:     // the data plane to the state prior to matching the first request into the bucket.\\n182:     //\\n183:     // **Restarting the subscription**\\n184:     //\\n185:     // If a new request is matched into a bucket previously abandoned, the data plane must behave\\n186:     // as if it has never tracked the bucket, and it's the first request matched into it:\\n187:     //\\n188:     // 1. The process of :ref:`subscription and reporting\\n189:     //    <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.rate_limit_quota.v3.RateLimitQuotaBucketSettings.reporting_interval>`\\n190:     //    starts from the beginning.\\n191:     //\\n192:     // 2. The bucket transitions to the :ref:`\\\"no assignment\\\"\\n193:     //    <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.rate_limit_quota.v3.RateLimitQuotaBucketSettings.no_assignment_behavior>`\\n194:     //    state.\\n195:     //\\n196:     // 3. The actions are applied in the\\n228:   // given order, from top to bottom.\\n229:   repeated BucketAction bucket_action = 1 [(validate.rules).repeated = {min_items: 1}];\\n230: }\\n231: \\n232: // The identifier for the bucket. Indicates that the RLQS server will no longer be\n170:     // sending updates for the given :ref:`bucket_id\n171:     // <envoy_v3_api_field_service.rate_limit_quota.v3.RateLimitQuotaResponse.BucketAction.bucket_id>`.\n172:     //\n173:     // If no requests are reported for a bucket, after some time the server considers the bucket\n174:     // inactive. The server stops tracking the bucket, and instructs the the data plane to abandon\n175:     // the bucket via this message.\n176:     //\n177:     // **Abandoning the assignment**\n178:     //\n179:     // The data plane is to erase the bucket (including its usage data) from the memory.\n180:     // It should stop tracking the bucket, and stop reporting its usage. This effectively resets\n181:     // the data plane to the state prior to matching the first request into the bucket.\n182:     //\n183:     // **Restarting the subscription**\n184:     //\n185:     // If a new request is matched into a bucket previously abandoned, the data plane must behave\n186:     // as if it has never tracked the bucket, and it's the first request matched into it:\n187:     //\n188:     // 1. Once the new assignment is received, it's applied per\n197:     //    \"Applying the first assignment to the bucket\" section of the :ref:`QuotaAssignmentAction\n198:     //    <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.rate_limit_quota.v3.RateLimitQuotaResponse.BucketAction.QuotaAssignmentAction>`.\n199:     message AbandonAction {\n200:     }\n201: \n202:     // ``BucketId`` for which request the action is applied.\n203:     BucketId bucket_id = 1 [(validate.rules).message = {required: true}];\n204: \n205:     oneof bucket_action {\n206:       option (validate.required) = true;\n207: \n208:       // Apply the quota assignment to the bucket.\n209:       //\n210:       // Commands the data plane to apply a rate limiting strategy to the bucket.\n211:       // The process of applying and expiring the rate limiting strategy is detailed in the\n212:       // :ref:`QuotaAssignmentAction\n213:       // <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.rate_limit_quota.v3.RateLimitQuotaResponse.BucketAction.QuotaAssignmentAction>`\n214:       // message.\n215:       QuotaAssignmentAction quota_assignment_action = 2;\n216: \n217:       // Abandon the bucket.\n218:       //\n219:       // Commands the data plane to abandon the bucket.\n220:       // The process of abandoning the bucket is described in the :ref:`AbandonAction\n221:       // <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.rate_limit_quota.v3.RateLimitQuotaResponse.BucketAction.AbandonAction>`\n222:       // message.\n223:       AbandonAction abandon_action = 3;\n224:     }\n225:   }\n226: \n227:   // An ordered list of actions to be applied to the buckets.
